  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_7bcd3cc4-5fe8-49b9-9fa9-6a347d2d602b'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2177708010" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2080907974528901034"><b><u> THIS IS NOT</u> a whole book</b><br/><br/>It's like someone ripped out the middle of the story and threw a cover around it. <br/><br/>The beginning was pretty much non-existent (essentially, the "beginning" was book 8) and the ending was another big fat TO BE CONTINUED... <br/><br/>How hard would it be to make these books a bit longer so we don't continuously run into this? <br/><br/>And when they <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ offed Mr. Crepsley <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> are you kidding me??<br/><br/> The whole fake-out just yanked my emotional cord like a yo-yo. I haven't f</span>
  <span id="freeText2080907974528901034" style="display:none"><b><u> THIS IS NOT</u> a whole book</b><br /><br />It's like someone ripped out the middle of the story and threw a cover around it. <br /><br />The beginning was pretty much non-existent (essentially, the "beginning" was book 8) and the ending was another big fat TO BE CONTINUED... <br /><br />How hard would it be to make these books a bit longer so we don't continuously run into this? <br /><br />And when they <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ offed Mr. Crepsley <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> are you kidding me??<br /><br /> The whole fake-out just yanked my emotional cord like a yo-yo. I haven't felt that betrayed by an author in a long time. This ending made continuing with the series nearly insurmountable.<br /><br /><b>Audiobook Comments</b><br />Read by Ralph Lister - and he did a pretty fab job of it.<br /><br /><a href="http://bit.ly/33ii2CT" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | Snapchat @miranda.reads <br /><br />Happy Reading!</span>

<div id="review_27529238" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/27529238" />
    <a title="Ahmad Sharabiani" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/614778-ahmad-sharabiani"><img alt="Ahmad Sharabiani" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1194930432p2/614778.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/27529238?book_show_action=true">Jul 17, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ahmad Sharabiani" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ahmad Sharabiani" href="/user/show/614778-ahmad-sharabiani">Ahmad Sharabiani</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007137817" href="/book/show/164729.Killers_of_the_Dawn">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=childrens-young-readers">childrens-young-readers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=irish">irish</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=21th-century">21th-century</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer27529238" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10162286985123233283"><b>Killers of the Dawn (Cirque du Freak #9), Darren Shan</b><br/><br/>Killers of the Dawn is the ninth book in The Saga of Darren Shan by Darren Shan (his real name, Darren O'Shaughnessy). It is also the third book in the Vampire War trilogy. <br/><br/>It also continues the events of Allies of the Night which leaves Darren meeting his ex-girlfriend, Debbie and his ex-bestfriend, Steve Leonard, who is later revealed to be a half vampaneze. <br/><br/>Mr. Crepsley, Darren, and Harkat go into the tunnels, where they find Vancha. They a</span>
  <span id="freeText10162286985123233283" style="display:none"><b>Killers of the Dawn (Cirque du Freak #9), Darren Shan</b><br /><br />Killers of the Dawn is the ninth book in The Saga of Darren Shan by Darren Shan (his real name, Darren O'Shaughnessy). It is also the third book in the Vampire War trilogy. <br /><br />It also continues the events of Allies of the Night which leaves Darren meeting his ex-girlfriend, Debbie and his ex-bestfriend, Steve Leonard, who is later revealed to be a half vampaneze. <br /><br />Mr. Crepsley, Darren, and Harkat go into the tunnels, where they find Vancha. They arm themselves with weapons carelessly discarded by the Vampaneze and seek out Steve. <br /><br />Steve calls the rest of the Vampaneze. There is a battle between the Vampaneze and the vampires, and soon they face the Vampaneze Lord. The Vampaneze Lord says that he and Mr. Crepsley must fight one another alone with no help from anyone. <br /><br />The Vampaneze and Vampires stop their fighting. At last Mr. Crepsley kills the Vampaneze Lord, but Steve jumps onto his back and causes him to fall over the cliff, where he is hanging over the pit of flaming stakes with Steve. Since he believes the Vampaneze Lord is dead, he agrees to kill himself and stop holding on to Steve in exchange for rest. <br /><br />Mr. Crepsley lets go of Steve and falls into the pit below, giving Darren a smile as they've succeeded in ending the war. After he is dead and everyone has safely departed, Steve reveals himself to Darren as the Vampaneze Lord: the one whom Darren or Vancha must destroy for the sake of the world. Mr. Crepsley's death had been in vain, which leaves Darren devastated and feeling empty.<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: ماه آگوست سال 2006میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: قصه های سرزمین اشباح: جلد نهم قاتلان سحر؛ نویسنده دارن شان؛ مترجم: فرزانه کریمی؛ سوده کریمی، تهران، قدیانی، بنفشه، 1383؛ در 224ص؛ موضوع داستانهای نویسندگان ایرلندی - سده 20م<br /><br />دارن شان شاهزاده اشباح، به خاطر مردمش باید در مبارزه ای خونبار شرکت کند؛ حیله های رذیلانه تر و سرکشتر از همیشه دست به کار شده اند؛ در این میان پلیس و مردم وحشتزده نیز او را و دوستانش را عامل کشتارهای هولناک شهر میدانند؛ تبلیغات پشت جلد کتاب<br /><br />استیو لئوپارد ماهیت حقیقی خود را آشکار میکند و شکست میخورد اما ارباب شبه واره ها فرار میکند و ...؛<br /><br />تاریخ بهنگام رسانی 22/08/1399هجری خورشیدی؛ ا. شربیانی</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16282428940719206625"><div><p>Picks up right where <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8966.Allies_of_the_Night__Cirque_du_Freak___8_' title='Allies of the Night (Cirque du Freak, #8) by Darren Shan' rel='nofollow noopener'>Allies of the Night</a> left off and I mean right where it left off. Like you could have turned the page and started a new chapter. There is a prologue to remind you where Allies of the Night ended and then you're right into the story.</p> <p>This episode of Cirque du Freak, and that's how you really have to think of it, was short and exciting but predictable. There was really no more character building. After this many books, the author doesn't have much more to offer in guess. I trul</p></div></span>
  <span id="freeText16282428940719206625" style="display:none"><div><p>Picks up right where <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8966.Allies_of_the_Night__Cirque_du_Freak___8_" title="Allies of the Night (Cirque du Freak, #8) by Darren Shan" rel="nofollow noopener">Allies of the Night</a> left off and I mean right where it left off. Like you could have turned the page and started a new chapter. There is a prologue to remind you where Allies of the Night ended and then you're right into the story.</p> <p>This episode of Cirque du Freak, and that's how you really have to think of it, was short and exciting but predictable. There was really no more character building. After this many books, the author doesn't have much more to offer in guess. I truly believe these books would be much better if combined into longer complete novels instead of the episodes they are now. I don't see the point in sitting down for an hour to simply read the next episode. Let me choose how much I want to read instead of force feeding me little chunks of your story. I just find it annoying and at this point, I'm not sure I'm interested in continuing. The latest reveal was like "well duh who didn't see that coming" and what's the point of read books like that?</p><br /></div></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer119688522&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer119688522" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17672850274905203498">OH MY LORD. This book was amazing. The last few chapters were INTENSE. Really, really excellent. <br/><br/>I had a hunch from the 8th book that Steve was the Vampaneze Lord, but I set that theory aside when he was said to be a friend. Even after it was found out that he was a villian, the others saw the lord themselves, so I just tosted the theory out the window. But in the ending, this theory came back to me as a full-fledged fact, and slapped me in the face.<br/><br/>The worst, and most epic part, was when Mr. Cr</span>
  <span id="freeText17672850274905203498" style="display:none">OH MY LORD. This book was amazing. The last few chapters were INTENSE. Really, really excellent. <br /><br />I had a hunch from the 8th book that Steve was the Vampaneze Lord, but I set that theory aside when he was said to be a friend. Even after it was found out that he was a villian, the others saw the lord themselves, so I just tosted the theory out the window. But in the ending, this theory came back to me as a full-fledged fact, and slapped me in the face.<br /><br />The worst, and most epic part, was when Mr. Crepsley died. For a page or two Darren fooled me into thinking that everything was alright, that they were saved...<br /><br />...and then in the next chapter he said. "That's not how it happened. But I sure wished that's how it did."<br /><br />When I read that, my blood froze. I couldn't believe it. Mr. Crepsley - dead. I'm not even sure if I can continue the series now - that dude was one of my favorite characters, second to Darren. All the readers have known him since the beginning, and how his relationship with Darren went from hate to best friends - practically brothers. To have him die like that - when I know him so well - saddened me. Characters' deaths are terrible to get over; it's like the death of Fred Weasly all over again. (JK...Rowling!) And the fact that he died in vain, and was so close to killing so REAL Vampaneze Lord, made everything just more horrific. It makes me mad to think that Mr. Crepsley could have LIVED and he chose to DIE honorably, but for the wrong thing! God darnit...<br /><br />Loved the book, though. This author has the awesome ability to make action scenes fun to read and...exciting. Not sure what the next books will be bring, but there's no doubt there will be more sorrow.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17672850274905203498" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Etienne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Etienne" href="/user/show/11486904-etienne">Etienne</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3198935308" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8238430478160351326">3,5/5. Not the best one of the series for sure. It has a good cliff hanger, like always so of course I want to push on reading the series which is very good, but this book as a standalone, felt a bit long, even if it,s really short, a bit repetitive and not much character development. It felt like the book is overstretch and by the way overstretching the series. The main problem I have was that for most of the book a character, a vampire, is very concern and bother by a sprained ankle... I mean </span>
  <span id="freeText8238430478160351326" style="display:none">3,5/5. Not the best one of the series for sure. It has a good cliff hanger, like always so of course I want to push on reading the series which is very good, but this book as a standalone, felt a bit long, even if it,s really short, a bit repetitive and not much character development. It felt like the book is overstretch and by the way overstretching the series. The main problem I have was that for most of the book a character, a vampire, is very concern and bother by a sprained ankle... I mean he is a vampire, and old one, how could that bother him so much for so long... When we could have been trough a very intense confrontation, we failed a bit short, avoiding it, running from it and it let me own a bit. I know this might sound really bad, but the book is still fun, but the series was such a hit with almost every books so far that my expectation are really high and this one didn't reach them totally.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8238430478160351326" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3164938673" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3164938673" />
    <a title="Alyssia Cooke" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5793303-alyssia-cooke"><img alt="Alyssia Cooke" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1310580876p2/5793303.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3164938673?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alyssia Cooke" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alyssia Cooke" href="/user/show/5793303-alyssia-cooke">Alyssia Cooke</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5793303-alyssia-cooke?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5793303-alyssia-cooke?shelf=children">children</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5793303-alyssia-cooke?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5793303-alyssia-cooke?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3164938673" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3153599096085900776">Much of this was really quite exciting and action packed, although I still think that these books would be better combining at least two books into one so that they aren't these really short snippets, ultimately always ending on a cliffhanger. Either way, we start right where we left off in the previous book - always a key tell that they should really be a single entity -with Darren still reeling from a betrayal. Things are only going to get worse for our ragtag group of heroes as before long th</span>
  <span id="freeText3153599096085900776" style="display:none">Much of this was really quite exciting and action packed, although I still think that these books would be better combining at least two books into one so that they aren't these really short snippets, ultimately always ending on a cliffhanger. Either way, we start right where we left off in the previous book - always a key tell that they should really be a single entity -with Darren still reeling from a betrayal. Things are only going to get worse for our ragtag group of heroes as before long the police turn up, suspecting them of being the killers who have been plaguing the city.<br /><br />I enjoyed this refreshing bout of the real world coming face to face with things beyond their ability to understand or control. Their guilt is all but assured when the police find the body of a dead Vampet in the house, tortured for information. The pace really picks up here and I liked how various characters are played with. The ending took a bit of a dismal turn and I particularly did not enjoy the make believe scene where you are assured that all's well that end's well, only to have Darren say, 'I wish that's what happened'. That was a cheap tactic and more than a little annoying.<br /><br />Either way, this is an action packed adventure. There is definite violence and brutality here even if it isn't described in vivid detail. I'd say it's a children's book, but one that I'd likely recommend to those twelve and above.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3153599096085900776" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3988279757120204083">I feel so let down. I've been pretty much enjoying this series even though the first one wasn't so good. The writing in this one reminded me of the first one. First of all I thought they were being all original when they didn't do the predictable thing and make Darren's sworn enemy show up as the leader of the bad guys. His sworn enemy was only a protector of the leader of the bad guys. I thought it was cool they were breaking the mold and that the author had tricked me. Too bad it turned out th</span>
  <span id="freeText3988279757120204083" style="display:none">I feel so let down. I've been pretty much enjoying this series even though the first one wasn't so good. The writing in this one reminded me of the first one. First of all I thought they were being all original when they didn't do the predictable thing and make Darren's sworn enemy show up as the leader of the bad guys. His sworn enemy was only a protector of the leader of the bad guys. I thought it was cool they were breaking the mold and that the author had tricked me. Too bad it turned out they did the little "ooh look, a revelation!" and did the predictable thing after all, and on top of that they ended the book happily and then you turn the page and it starts a new chapter with "I wish that had been what had happened," leading you into a horrific reversal of what you'd just read and ending with a very important character dying. Oh wonderful. That's just bad form, man. Bad form.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16566702336675502119">I do enjoy this series. I SWEAR!! But the way these books have been paced have confused me so much. The action in this book is fun and very fast paced. I feel like our three hunters (Crepsley, Darren, and Vancha) are facing off against the Vampaneze the entire time. Every turn they make has something else crop up for them to deal with (people learning that vampires are real, the cop thinking they're lying, angry mobs in apartment complexes....)<br/><br/>But the past two books were slow. This book is makes</span>
  <span id="freeText16566702336675502119" style="display:none">I do enjoy this series. I SWEAR!! But the way these books have been paced have confused me so much. The action in this book is fun and very fast paced. I feel like our three hunters (Crepsley, Darren, and Vancha) are facing off against the Vampaneze the entire time. Every turn they make has something else crop up for them to deal with (people learning that vampires are real, the cop thinking they're lying, angry mobs in apartment complexes....)<br /><br />But the past two books were slow. This book is makes up for a lot of the slowness of the past few books. There is STILL a lot for the hunters to face before defeating the Vampaneze Lord.<br /><br />And lets talk about <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Crepsley dying! my heart hurts. And now Darren's mentor is GONE <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and we have 3 books left. WHAT</span>

<div id="review_279611591" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/279611591" />
    <a title="Whitney" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4881155-whitney"><img alt="Whitney" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1439004129p2/4881155.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/279611591?book_show_action=true">Feb 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Whitney" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Whitney" href="/user/show/4881155-whitney">Whitney</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316106" href="/book/show/7895541-killers-of-the-dawn">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4881155-whitney?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4881155-whitney?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4881155-whitney?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4881155-whitney?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4881155-whitney?shelf=supernatural">supernatural</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4881155-whitney?shelf=male-protagonist">male-protagonist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4881155-whitney?shelf=four-stars">four-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer279611591" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17344005774649588477">After the betrayal at the hands of his once best friend, Darren Shan finds himself in boiling water. He, along with Mr. Crepsley, Harkat, and Vancha, are framed for the murders the vampaneze were committing. Now they’ve got the humans and vampaneze wanting to spill their blood. This might be the end for Darren and his allies.<br/><br/><b>Plot</b><br/><br/>I was pleasantly surprised with <i>Killers of the Dawn</i>. The past couple of books have been a real snooze fest. That’s all changed in this book. The plot is fast paced and t</span>
  <span id="freeText17344005774649588477" style="display:none">After the betrayal at the hands of his once best friend, Darren Shan finds himself in boiling water. He, along with Mr. Crepsley, Harkat, and Vancha, are framed for the murders the vampaneze were committing. Now they’ve got the humans and vampaneze wanting to spill their blood. This might be the end for Darren and his allies.<br /><br /><b>Plot</b><br /><br />I was pleasantly surprised with <i>Killers of the Dawn</i>. The past couple of books have been a real snooze fest. That’s all changed in this book. The plot is fast paced and there’s plenty of action. And instead of nothing plot wise happening, the story is finally moving forward again. And not a moment too soon! There’s only three books left and so I had hoped the plot would chug along soon. It did, with Darren and company running from the police and battling the vampaneze. There aren’t a lot of dull moments in <i>Killers of the Dawn</i>. It’s like I’m being rewarded for mucking through three slow action-less books. <br /><br /><b>Writing</b><br /><br />Since this book was mostly action and fast paced things, Shan’s writing really had a chance to shine. He’s very good at writing tense scenes. There were a few scenes where nothing happened, but since they were sandwiched between actions they weren’t that hard to get through. I also have to applaud Shan on the little hints he drops throughout <i>Allies of the Night</i> and <i>Killers of the Dawn</i> that are important to the plot twist at the end of the book. And observant reader could have probably caught then. I didn’t when I first read through the series. Either way, the plot twist at the end of the book was great and I was completely blindsided the first time I read the book. This time I was prepared but I also noticed more things. Kudos, Darren Shan.<br /><br /><b>Characters</b><br /><br />Darren continues to act like a child in some cases. For example, when they are running from the police and they break into Richard’s house, he develops a sudden conscious and states that they can’t stay, despite being chased by police and an angry mob, because Richard didn’t <i>give them permission</i> to stay. This was utterly silly and a goof like that could have cost them big time. <br /><br />There is an important character death, though I won’t mention who. Unfortunately, I didn’t feel much when they died. Though they had a good relationship with Darren, the development of the relationship didn’t make me feel sad that Darren was without them now. I was sad that Darren lost them and quite shocked that the character had died, but their death didn’t mean all that much to me emotionally because as the reader I didn’t feel as connected to them.<br /><br /> <b>Things I Didn't Like</b><br /><br />I was actually quite pleased with <i>Killers of the Dawn</i>. I suppose the only thing I didn’t like was how things went down with the police. For example, the police said they got an anonymous tip from a person from a telephone booth and then proceeded to post nearly two hundred officers around the building Darren and company were hiding out in. This doesn’t make sense. Anonymous tips aren’t taken <i>that</i> seriously. I found that part hard to accept. That was pretty much it, though.<br /><br /><b>Diversity</b><br /><br />Debbie, our only character of color, was held hostage for nearly the entire book, only to be seen again near the end. On the bright side, we get to see a little of a new female character, Police Chief Inspector Alice Burgess. She’s a strong woman and I liked her for the little role she played in the book. I hope to see more of her in action.<br /><br /><b>Overall</b><br /><br />I loved <i>Killers of the Dawn</i>. It was fast-paced, full of action, and full of twists and turns. Readers might guess what they are, but I think they can still appreciate them. I know I did. The end of the series is in sight and if the last three books are like this one, it’ll be great. <br /><br /><a href="http://booknoting.tumblr.com/post/117309388520/killers-of-the-dawn-notes" rel="nofollow noopener">Here is a link to my notes.</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="17344005774649588477" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5774490466402901083">Ya you know the typical vampire storys where the average vampire drinks blood and can turn into a bat and fly away. But this is not one of those storys this is a story about a boy (that is at least 30) that does not age as fast as we do and doesnt turn into a bat and fly away when they feel like there losing a battle. No this is a book about Darren Shan a vampires assistent that will soon be a ex-vampires assistent. But before I can tell you that I have to tell you about everything else leading </span>
  <span id="freeText5774490466402901083" style="display:none">Ya you know the typical vampire storys where the average vampire drinks blood and can turn into a bat and fly away. But this is not one of those storys this is a story about a boy (that is at least 30) that does not age as fast as we do and doesnt turn into a bat and fly away when they feel like there losing a battle. No this is a book about Darren Shan a vampires assistent that will soon be a ex-vampires assistent. But before I can tell you that I have to tell you about everything else leading up to that. Assuming you have read all the other books they have gone back to Mr. Creapsly's home town and are looking for the vampanise lord. <br /><br />They have ben told that if they kill this vampanise lord they will win the war of scars (war between vampires and vampanise). They were told that they will have very few chances to kill this lord. They have used three now they will miss there forth. One night Darren was walking to the hotel he was staying at and he is confronted by a vampanise he was losing the fight and just before he was going to die and gun was fired and the vampanise was hit but not killed so he took off and the man who had saved darren pointed the gun at him and said "I know what you are" and darren instanly knew the voise. It was his old fraind Steve! <br /><br />Ya I know crazy right and thats not even the good part th good part is when Steve turns on him and he is in leage with the vampanise. So they are drawn down into the sewers and that is when the battle begins! They are out numbered and they have no way out but to fight there way out Mr. Crepsly (Darrens mentore) has put his life on the line to fight the vampanise lord who was whaching the battle from a ledge a ways away. Mr. Crepsly ran across the bridge and then they engage on an epic battle in which two will die. Before I tell you what happens you have to read the book.<br /><br />Now that you have read the book I will tell you Mr. Creapsly kills the vampanise lord by throwing him down into the firey pit of staks and then Steve dose a full on tackle into Mr. Creapsly an Creapsly is falling into the pit of staks but is holding onto Steves weapon and is intent on bringing him down with him! But Vancas brother grabes Steves other arm and is the only thing between him Steve and Mr. Creaplsy is the firey staks that will soon clame a life. Then Vancas brother proposes a deal Mr. Creaplsy will fall and Steves life will be spared along with Darren and Vancas and everyone else in the cavern. Mr. Creapsly takes the deal and lets go of Steve and he falls into the pit of firey staks. Crazy I know one of the main charicters dies right there and taht is not even the end! After the big battle Steve goes up to Darren and tells him the truth! He whispers into Darrens ear and then Darren begins to yell out but then he is put out by vancas brother so that they can escape! When Darren comes too he tells Vanca that Mr. Creapsly died in vain. STEVE WAS THE VAMPANINSE LORD!<br /><br />I really enjoyed this book and am now reading the next book. If I had to recomend a book this serese would be it!It has amazing action and is full of uniqe suprises like the one I have just had! I hope to finish the seres by the end of the year and I also hope that they will be full of action like this one has been. But my question is how will the aurther make it as fun as all the others without Mr. Creapsly!<br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_1114377738" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1114377738" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1114377738?book_show_action=true">Nov 24, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1114377738" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14523671990595965677"> I liked the book, but I like all the books by Darren Shan. He really knows how to keep a reader on the edge of their seats and on edge just waiting to see how the problem will be resolved. Another reason that Darren is one of my favorite authors is that he can enthuse a reader within the first two chapters, that is how I got hooked to his books. He is an amazing author with an amazing imagination on how the characters should act and live or die. He has been able to capture the interests of othe</span>
  <span id="freeText14523671990595965677" style="display:none"> I liked the book, but I like all the books by Darren Shan. He really knows how to keep a reader on the edge of their seats and on edge just waiting to see how the problem will be resolved. Another reason that Darren is one of my favorite authors is that he can enthuse a reader within the first two chapters, that is how I got hooked to his books. He is an amazing author with an amazing imagination on how the characters should act and live or die. He has been able to capture the interests of other amazing authors as well such as Alexander Gordon Smith, and other very interesting authors. <br /><br /> Darren has changed a lot since being blooded as a prince of the vampire clan about six or so years ago back at Vampire Mountain when he warned everyone about the Vampaneze who were hiding out in the tunnels of the mountain. Since being blooded as a Prince, Darren has felt less guilt with killing Vampaneze. The first time that Darren had killed a Vampaneze, he felt so guilty because the Vampaneze was only a few years older than he was. After he killed him he did not want to drag out the killing anymore until he seen that Ara Sails a friend and ex-mate of Mr. Crepsley was in trouble and needed help. Killers of the Dawn is the 9th book of the Cirque Du Freak series and picks up after the little battle between the Hunters who are the two Vampire Princes, Darren Shan, Vancha March and the non-prince mentor of Darren's, Mr. Crepsley, who are the vampaneze lord Steve Leonard who was Darren's childhood friend before joining the ranks of the undead with Mr. Crepsley. The vampires have a prophecy that when the vampaneze lord is revealed, three vampires must hunt him down and kill him so that they may win the war of the scars. Only the hunters may be able to kill the Vampaneze for if someone else does the Vampaneze will win the war.<br /><br /> Darren has really grown up since being blooded as a Vampire Prince. He has grown into his throne by killing the vampaneze. He has really come to accept the fact that there is no way to go back to being human. <br /><br /> The setting at the beginning of the book, Darren is back in the tunnels of blood with Mr. Crepsley and old friend Harkat Mulds. There was never a time period given, but I would have to guess it was modern times because they were using cell phones and guns. They are once again looking for the Vampaneze Lord. The tunnels of blood are located underneath Mr. Crepsley's old home town. The first time Darren was in the town, he was with Mr. Crepsley and his cirque friend Evra Von the Snake boy. The first time they were chasing a mad vampaneze named Mourlough. They had killed Mourlough when they had hunted and found him in the tunnels. <br /><br /> If I had to recommend this book to anyone, it would probably have to be for people who can handle gory scenes and some really bad profanity. It would be for people of ages 14 and up, and if I had to choose a gender it would probably have to be male.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14523671990595965677" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer77244548" class="readable"

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16012757826096608798">Oh <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5816.Darren_Shan' title='Darren Shan' rel='nofollow noopener'>Darren Shan</a> how you break my heart with these books! Even though I thought I was prepared for the series to end, even knowing the plight of the hero... I was still not ready for this book!<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <em><strong>Summary:</strong> Outnumbered, outsmarted and desperate, the hunters are on the run, pursued by the vampaneze, the police, and an angry mob. With their enemies clamoring for blood, the vampires prepare for a deadly battle. Is this the end for Darren and his allies?</em>
</blockquote><br/><br/><strong>What I liked about this book:</strong> <u>
  <strong>SPOILER ALERT: T</strong></u></span>
  <span id="freeText16012757826096608798" style="display:none">Oh <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5816.Darren_Shan" title="Darren Shan" rel="nofollow noopener">Darren Shan</a> how you break my heart with these books! Even though I thought I was prepared for the series to end, even knowing the plight of the hero... I was still not ready for this book!<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em><strong>Summary:</strong> Outnumbered, outsmarted and desperate, the hunters are on the run, pursued by the vampaneze, the police, and an angry mob. With their enemies clamoring for blood, the vampires prepare for a deadly battle. Is this the end for Darren and his allies?</em>
</blockquote><br /><br /><strong>What I liked about this book:</strong> <u>
  <strong>SPOILER ALERT: THIS REVIEW CONTAINS SPOILERS FOR THE SERIES. DO NOT READ IF YOU DO NOT WANT TO KNOW.</strong>
  <u> I had to put this one down just as I realized what the end of this book would hold just as I put <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1.Harry_Potter_and_the_Half_Blood_Prince__Harry_Potter___6_" title="Harry Potter and the Half-Blood Prince (Harry Potter, #6) by J.K. Rowling" rel="nofollow noopener">Harry Potter and the Half-Blood Prince</a> down as it became evident that Harry would finish his journey without Dumbledore. While <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5816.Darren_Shan" title="Darren Shan" rel="nofollow noopener">Darren Shan</a>'s characters don't ingrain themselves into my psyche as much as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1077326.J_K__Rowling" title="J.K. Rowling" rel="nofollow noopener">J.K. Rowling</a>'s do, they still come to life in that way that you root for them, suffer with them and feel yourself drawn to them in the way only a good author can do. <br /><br />Losing loved ones is expected in a vampire book. The sheer fact that as a vampire you outlive those you love is, in and of itself, a prophetic fact to that loss. But losing a mentor, losing that being who charts you on the path and becomes more than a teacher and a guide, becomes the father-figure, the best friend and confidante every hero needs, is much more tragic. You feel it deep in your heart and watching Larten Crepsley fall made it very difficult for me to devour this book.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5816.Darren_Shan" title="Darren Shan" rel="nofollow noopener">Darren Shan</a> has an ability to make you feel what his main character feels in such a battle-torn way that you not only feel the toll of the battle on your soul, you feel its repercussions for a long time. I may need some time to recoup before diving into the last three books.</u>
</u></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer19922980" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15566189858080288236">The vampires continue to fight the ongoing war with the vampeneze, the War of the Scars as it is to be known. The vampaneze are an evil race of vampires who broke off from the Council hundreds of years ago and don't follow any of the vampire's rules of conduct; in particular, they have no respect for human lives. <br/><br/>As prophesied by Mr. Tiny, the three vampire hunters—Darren, Mr. Crepsley, and Vancha March—must defeat the Lord of the Vampeneze in one of four potential encounters. The fate of the en</span>
  <span id="freeText15566189858080288236" style="display:none">The vampires continue to fight the ongoing war with the vampeneze, the War of the Scars as it is to be known. The vampaneze are an evil race of vampires who broke off from the Council hundreds of years ago and don't follow any of the vampire's rules of conduct; in particular, they have no respect for human lives. <br /><br />As prophesied by Mr. Tiny, the three vampire hunters—Darren, Mr. Crepsley, and Vancha March—must defeat the Lord of the Vampeneze in one of four potential encounters. The fate of the entire vampire race depends on the outcome of this war; for if they <i>do not</i> manage to kill the Vampeneze Lord, then the vampires will perish, and the vampenze will rule.<br /><br />The hunters, along with Little Person Harkat Mulds, have already let the Lord of the Vampenze slip through their hands once. So now they have only three more chances to defeat him. Unfortunately for Darren and the hunters, they don't even know the true identity of the Vampaneze Lord, and they have no idea what he looks like either, so their task is quite difficult! There's also several surprises and a few sad endings in store in this one....<br /><br /><i>Killers of the Dawn</i> picks up right where the previous book, <i>
  <a href="http://books.cheriepie.com/2008/01/73-cirque-du-freak-8-allies-of-night-by.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Allies of the Night</a>
</i>, left off. With this series, there's sometimes be a little break in action between books; but at other times, you're left at a cliffhanger and the next book picks up right where the previous one left off, often at the very same scene. The latter has been the case with the last few books.<br /><br />Like all the previous books, I really enjoyed this one too. It was quick and action-packed. Plus there's some really neat revelations beginning to come out! *shhh* LOL I really wanted to start on the tenth book, <i>The Lake of Souls</i>, right after I finished this, but for a change, there actually seemed to be a bit of a break at the end. So instead, I'm holding off while I catch up on some other reading, and then plan to finish the series with books ten through twelve all in one fell swoop, since I do have the remaining three waiting on Mt. TBR. :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="15566189858080288236" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9919727257646804842">The book starts with Darren and his friends quickly leaving the underground passages to escape the Vampaneze and vampets. With them are two hostages, Steve Leopard (who reveals himself to be a half-vampaneze) and a vampet. Debbie has been taken hostage by R.V., Vancha tortures the vampet back at their base and finds out that only the Vampaneze Lord can kill the three hunters. Unfortunately, Steve had arranged for the police to find out about them and soon they are surrounded by the police and ar</span>
  <span id="freeText9919727257646804842" style="display:none">The book starts with Darren and his friends quickly leaving the underground passages to escape the Vampaneze and vampets. With them are two hostages, Steve Leopard (who reveals himself to be a half-vampaneze) and a vampet. Debbie has been taken hostage by R.V., Vancha tortures the vampet back at their base and finds out that only the Vampaneze Lord can kill the three hunters. Unfortunately, Steve had arranged for the police to find out about them and soon they are surrounded by the police and army. They escape by jumping through the window, while Vancha escapes with the chief of police; the rest are captured and imprisoned. Eventually a vampet called Morgan helps Darren escape, claiming that he is proud to serve the creatures of the night. Darren then helps Harkat escape, a task which was aided by the guards' fear of Harkat (they were under the impression that he had a rare and deadly disease). The two together are able to free Larten Crepsley. They quickly go outside, unnoticed by the guards who are occupied by Steve's having killed a nurse and two other people. Mr. Crepsley, Darren and Harkat descend into the tunnels, where they meet up with Vancha. They arm themselves with weapons carelessly discarded by the vampaneze. They seek out Steve, who calls the rest of the vampaneze. There is a battle between the two sides, and soon they face whom they believe is the Vampaneze Lord. The suspected Vampaneze Lord says that he and Mr. Crepsley must fight one another alone. Crepsley kills the Vampaneze Lord, but Steve jumps onto his back and causes him to fall over the side, where he is hanging over the flaming stakes with Steve. Since he believes the Vampaneze lord is dead, he agrees to kill himself and stop holding on to Steve in exchange for a free passage for the rest. After he is dead and everyone has safely departed, Steve reveals himself to Darren as the Vampaneze Lord: the one who Darren must destroy for the sake of the world.<br /><br /><br /></span>

So many feelings i don't know wither to be upset, surprised or scream at the book in hatred! <br /> However, saying that a brilliant book! The last few chapters where just wow. I just didn't know what to do when reading it I was like what just happened! <br /> I mean Why Mr Crepsley???? why did that have to happen???? I was gobsmacked I just never saw it coming - (well played Mr Shan well played) <br /> But anyway back to business loved this book full of suspense and surprise by the end couldn't ask for anything better that way, now I know I am shouting praises and most will probably be wondering 'well if you loved it so much why only give it a four' - well I will tell you. If was the beginning of the book. The book to begin with dragged on, to the point I was beginning to wonder if anything was actually going to happen (which it did - by god it did!) it just took a while also I am very upset at the moment at what happened to Mr Crepsley. You just give us it straight and it's so quick you just don't know wither to cry BUT then you go ahead and do a two-three chapter giving us hope that all was saved and I'm laughing and so happy that Mr Crepsley is alive he was saved to then turn the page and BOOM! It wasn't to be! and the crying starts all over again! WHY!!??!! <br /><br />Moment over......... <br /><br /> To those readers who may find the start as boring as I did - PERSIST honestly it gets so much better! There are so many twists and turns that it just leaves you speechless! So yeah over all a brilliant book! :D <br /><br />P.S. I KNEW STEVE WAS THE VAMPANEZE LORD I KNEW IT!!!! I had figured it out a few books back but then doubt set in until this book! - again very clever Mr Shan very clever indeed!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4420548586585208322" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316106542" href="/book/show/1605208.Killers_of_the_Dawn">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer672822145" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9859463201480188329">I think this may be the book I love the most in the series so far, but also the one I hate the most. I won't say who but someone dies and I was devastated. Can't believe he did that! He certainly doesn't mind killing off his characters, but why is it always the ones I like the most?<br/><br/>Now I've dropped that bombshell, I will explain, the death doesn't happen until right near the end, but I knew it was coming for a couple of chapters. Up to that point this book was so exciting and well written, I was</span>
  <span id="freeText9859463201480188329" style="display:none">I think this may be the book I love the most in the series so far, but also the one I hate the most. I won't say who but someone dies and I was devastated. Can't believe he did that! He certainly doesn't mind killing off his characters, but why is it always the ones I like the most?<br /><br />Now I've dropped that bombshell, I will explain, the death doesn't happen until right near the end, but I knew it was coming for a couple of chapters. Up to that point this book was so exciting and well written, I was utterly absorbed, swept up and chucked around by it. I didn't want it to end. <br /><br />The big war is coming and Crepsley, Shan and March are back on the trail of the Vampaneze prince, accompanied of course by Harket. I haven't said it before, but I really like Harket and with every book he develops more and grows so much. He may be described as quite ugly, but you can't help but want to hug him. He's a bit like the 'Dobby' of this world!<br /><br />There are more old faces turning up and some are not going to give up easily. Big battles, cunning plots and devious manoeuvres , this book will have you gripping the pages so hard and desperate for more. If only that ending hadn't have gone like that! <br /><br />I need to finish this series, I can't get enough. :D</span>
  <a data-text-id="9859463201480188329" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_6823529'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6823529-great-classic-horror"><img alt="Great Classic Horror" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1348531340l/6823529._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('PfIQegC+uiAPGTM7pRza6DL84TTKNQhVhmtZlaqKdpShAivd9fzT/Z9k849dbXhP/TkVIhqISao1MWFSCWvynA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('1Mz8ua0KyGJEhhkc2DjvGib+nNhzSDKIp+MBhwfwrhNIPMceWEihv9T72aggSU296TtozqP1c3cUuTlApBEqGw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

Questa divisione governativa gestisce direttamente un istituto sul confine fra le province di Nagano e Yamanashi, il cui nome ufficiale è Liceo Kyokujitsu, ma che gli studenti di tutto il Giappone chiamano con timore riverenziale Yosai Gakuen, la Scuola Fortezza!\n\nSituato su un altopiano, circondato da dirupi scoscesi e da una giungla in cui si aggirano belve affamate, il liceo è un vero e proprio carcere-riformatorio in cui viene volutamente fatta valere la legge del più forte e dove le punizioni corporali sono all\'ordine del giorno, sia da parte del corpo insegnanti, sia da parte delle commissioni disciplinari formate dagli stessi studenti. Oltre a questo, una legge non scritta e non detta grave sul perimetro scolastico e per questo motivo gli studenti sono costantemente sotto pressione, temendo in continuazione di trasgredire a di rischiare quindi la pena capitale. \n\nIn questa atmosfera violenta e priva di speranza, tre nuovi studenti vengono portati all\'interno dell\'istituto correttivo. Il primo è Gentaro Matsuda, incolpato ingiustamente di aver violentato la figlia dell\'ex Ministro di Grazia e Giustizia; il secondo è Itsuki Takizawa, reo di aver trafugato ripetutamente costoso materiale didattico in oltre dieci scuole; il terzo è il taciturno Mei Mato, un individuo talmente pericoloso da dover essere tenuto costantemente in catene. \n\nDurante il difficile inserimento nella scuola, i tre fanno amicizia e alcuni segreti vengono a galla. Itsuki è in realtà una ragazza, che si è fatta arrestare per poter entrare al Liceo Kyokujitsu, dove suo fratello è sparito senza lasciar traccia. Mei Mato, inceve, è il triste frutto di esperimenti genetici perpetrati di nascosto dallo stesso Preside della scuola, volti a mutare uomini in super-creature mostruose, facendo leva sulle informazioni contenute nel patrimonio genetico umano.\n\nEddy Kurosaki, braccio destro del Preside, stimola Mei ad attivare la propria trasformazione, ma invece di mutare in forma di allosauro come previsto, il ragazzo diviene una creatura da incubo inarrestabile, che solo l\'intervento di Itsuki - segretamente innamorata di lei - riesce a placare. Si scopre così che Mei non è altro che il primo di una lunga serie di cloni del Preside e che il fratello di Itsuki è stato lobotomizzato. \n\nGentaro, intanto, ottiene la fiducia del rude \'Tessy\' Teshigawara, al quale chiede di aiutarlo a organizzare una rivolta degli studenti - e a liberare i suoi amici - con la collaborazione dei Cinque Demoni, violenti e pressoché inaffidabili capibanda scolastici.\n\nNel frattempo, l\'agente Pussy Galore, un\'infiltrata del governo, indaga sulle attività illecite del Preside, con il compito di fermarlo in qualsiasi modo. E proprio mentre la rivolta studentesca subisce violentissime repressioni, l\'operazione governativo-militare entra nella fase attiva con l\'invasione della scuola da parte delle truppe di Difesa Nazionale. Ma il Preside ha ancora un asso nella manica e, deciso a indagare sulla bizzarra mutazione imprevista di Mei, libera le Tre Creature, ragazzi trattati con la Chiave Divina e in grado di diventare dinosauri antropomorfi. <span id="freeTextContainer11746135364811971953">Librarian's note: Also writes books for adults under the name <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7790731.Darren_Dash' rel='nofollow noopener'>Darren Dash</a>. Shan</a> and Darren O'Shaughnessy.<br/><br/>Darren Shan (born July 2, 1972 in London, England) is the pen name of the Irish author Darren O'Shaughnessy, as well as the name of the protagonist of his book series The Saga of Darren Shan, also known as The Cirque Du Freak</span>
  <span id="freeText11746135364811971953" style="display:none">Librarian's note: Also writes books for adults under the name <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7790731.Darren_Dash" rel="nofollow noopener">Darren Dash</a>. And in the past he has released books for adults under the names <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1304819.D_B_Shan" rel="nofollow noopener">D.B. Shan</a> and Darren O'Shaughnessy.<br /><br />Darren Shan (born July 2, 1972 in London, England) is the pen name of the Irish author Darren O'Shaughnessy, as well as the name of the protagonist of his book series The Saga of Darren Shan, also known as The Cirque Du Freak Series in the United States. He is the author of the series The Demonata, The Saga of Larten Crepsley, and Zom-B. He has also released the stand-alone novel, The Thin Executioner, and the stand-alone short novels, Koyasan, and Hagurosan. Plus, for adults, he released The City Trilogy (originally under the name of D.B. Shan), and Lady of the Shades.. </span>
